тАШрдЕрдирд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╛рдЧрд╕реНрддреНрдпрдВ рдмрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред рдЕрдирд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрдВ рдмрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рд╢реНрд░реМрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╢реМрдирдХрдГ– рд╕реНрдирд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЬрдкреЗрджрдирд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрдВ рдирдорд╕реНрдХреГрддреНрдп рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдореН ред рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН рдзрдирдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рд╕реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐’ (рдЛрдЧреНрд╡рд┐. рез. резрелрей-резрелрек ) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

190
Br╠еhaspati
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
8 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Br╠еhaspati, the lord of formulations, is here presented as both producer and receiver of sacred speech and sound. This theme is established in the first verse, where my chants strengthen Br╠еhaspati, who himself is the тАЬleader of song.тАЭ The physi cal movement of words and soundтАФbetween mortals and gods, between earth and heavenтАФis a repeated theme in the hymn (see esp. vss. 2, 4, 7). The difficult verses 3 and 4 concern a particular kind of sacred sound, the signal-call (┼Ыlo╠Бka) that Br╠еhaspati launches daily, most likely a call announcing the sacrifice or some part of it.
The Br╠еhaspati depicted in this hymn is no mere gentle wordsmith, but militant and aggressive, compared to a bellowing bull (vs. 1), a fearsome wild beast (vss. 3, 4), a bird of prey (vs. 7). His words are missiles (vs. 4), and those who underestimate him and seek to exploit him receive his punishment (vs. 5).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Bс╣Ыhaspati For the hymn as a whole, see H.-P. Schmidt, Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra (1968), 72- 77 and passim.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Priests), augment by your hymns Bс╣Ыhaspati, who deserts not (his worshipper); the showerer (of benefits) the plural asant-tongued, the adorable; of whom resplendent gods and men, (the ministers) of the instrumental tutor of the sacrifice, emulous in sacred songs, proclaim (the praise).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bс╣Ыhaspati is here defined as mantrasya p─Бlayit─Бram, the protector of cherisher of the prayer

Jamison Brereton

With chants I will strengthen anew the unassailable bull of gladdening tongue, Br╠еhaspati,
the brightly shining leader of song to whom the gods and the mortals harken as he bellows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The main cl. verb vardhay─Б is entirely ambiguous between 2nd sg. imperative and 1st sg. subjunctive. With Renou and Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra) I opt for the 1st sg. subj., while Grassmann, Geldner, and Witzel Got┼Н take it as 2nd sg. impv. There are no implications either way.

Griffith

GLORIFY thou Brhaspati, the scatheless, who must be praised with hymns, sweet-tongued and mighty,
To whom as leader of the song, resplendent, worthy of lauds, both Gods and mortals listen.

Geldner

Den unerreichbaren Bullen mit der wohllautenden Zunge, den Brihaspati erbaue aufs neue mit Preisliedern, den gl├дnzenden Gesangesleiter, auf den G├╢tter und Sterbliche hinh├╢ren, wenn er seine Stimme erhebt!

Grassmann

Den unnahbaren Mann, der lieblich redet, Brihaspati erhebe neu mit Liedern, Den leuchtenden, dem, wenn Gesang er leitet und singt, die G├╢tter und die Menschen lauschen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe hymns of the (rainy) season are addressed to him, who is verily the creator (of the rain), and has granted it (to the prayers) of the devout; for that Bс╣Ыhaspati is the manifester (of all), the expansive wind that (dispensing) blessings has been produced for (the diffusion of) water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The hymns of the rainy season: с╣Ыtivy─Б = varс╣гarttu sambandhinyo v─Бcaс╕е, prayers connected with the season of the rain

Jamison Brereton

Words follow close upon him in proper sequence, like a gush that has been sent gushing from those serving the gods,
for Br╠еhaspati, far-ranging straightway through the wide spaces, has become equal to M─Бtari┼Ыvan in regard to truth.

Griffith

On him wait songs according to the season even as a stream of pious men set moving.
Brhaspati–for he laid out the expanses–was, at the sacrifice, vast Matarisvan.

Geldner

Ihm streben rechtzeitig die Reden zu, die wie ein Ergu├Я der Gottergebenen sich ergossen haben, denn dieser Brihaspati, stracks die weiten R├дume durchdringend, ward im rechten Werk ein zweiter Matarisvan.

Grassmann

Ihm huldigen die festlichen Ges├дnge, der wie ein Zug der Frommen sich ergossen, Brihaspati, denn er versch├╢nt die Welten, und kr├дftig war beim Opfer Matari├зvan.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe is ready (to accept) the offered praise, the presentation of the homage, the hymn, as the sun (is ready) to put forth his rays; by the acts of him whom the r─Бkс╣гasas (oppose not), the daily (revolving sun) exists, and he is strong as a fearful beast of prey.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He: or, the pronoun may apply to the yajam─Бna, who exerts himself to offer the praise, the oblation

Jamison Brereton

A praise song and an offering of reverence, as well as his signal-call, will he hold forth, like Savitar his two armsтАФ
(the call) that happens every day according to his will, (the call) of the undemonic, which is powerful like a fearsome wild beast.

Griffith

The praise, the verse that offers adoration, may he bring forth, as the Sun sends his arms out,
He who gives daily light through this God’s wisdom, strong as a dread wild beast, and inoffensive.

Geldner

Den Lobgesang und die dargebrachte Huldigung, den Ruf m├╢ge er wie Savitri die Arme erheben, der nach seinem Ratschlu├Я tagt├дglich stattfindet, der Ruf des Arglosen, furchtbar wie ein wildes Tier, gewaltig.

Grassmann

Und Lob und Preis und des Gebets Verrichtung streck er empor, wie Savitar die Arme, Der tageshell durch seines Geistes Kraft ist, des B├╢sen Zwingherr, wie ein L├╢we furchtbar.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗрдГ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд┐рдХрд╛ рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЧрд░реНрдЬрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдХреН рд╡рд╛ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдИрдпрддреЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдпреЛ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрддреНрдпреЛ рди рдЕрддрдирд╢реАрд▓ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдп рдЗрд╡ рдпрдХреНрд╖рднреГрддреН рдкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рджрдзрд╛рдирдГ рд╡рд┐рдЪреЗрддрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рдЪреЗрддрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдпрдВрд╕рддреН рдирд┐рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдлрд▓рдореН ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдореГрдЧрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╣рдиреНрддреБрдордиреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рд╣реЗрддрдпрдГ рди рдЖрдпреБрдзрд╛рдиреАрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдп рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗрдГ рдЗрдорд╛рдГ рд╣реЗрддрдпреЛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЖрдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рее тАШрдЪрд╡рд╛рдпреЛрдЧреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рди рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рдЕрд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдпрд╛рдиреН рдЖрдЧрддреНрдп рд╣рдиреНрддреНрд░реНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдорд╛рдпрд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдирд╕реБрд░рд╛рдиреН рджреНрдпреВрди рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рд╛рдиреН ред’ рдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рдзреНрд╡рдиреЛрдГреж’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. реи. рей. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ рее рддрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдзрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрднрд┐ рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рее рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрд░реНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gloryof this Bс╣Ыhaspati spreads through heaven and earth like the sun; receiving worship, and giving intelligence, he bestows (the rewards of sacrifice); like the weapons of the hunters, so these (weapons) of Bс╣Ыhaspati fall daily upon the workers of guile.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like the weapons of the hunters: mс╣Ыg─Бс╣З─Бm na hetayaс╕е = hantum anviс╣гyatam ─Бyudhan─лva, like the weapons of those seeking to kill

Jamison Brereton

When his signal-call speeds in heaven and on earth like a steed, the discriminating one [=Br╠еhaspati?], bringing wondrous apparitions, will control it, *like a steedтАФ
as also when these missiles [=words] of Br╠еhaspati, like the charges of wild beasts, go to the heavens that possess serpentine wiles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are a number of syntactic questions and problems in this verse. To begin with, in p─Бda a the sequence div─л╠Бyate could be resolved as either div├н ─лyate (so Grassmann, Pp.) or div├н ─л╠Бyate. In the latter case, with accented verb, we could have a subordination without an overt subordinator. I have chosen to interpret it so, contra the standard tr. and interpr. (though with Scarlatta 371 n. 516), because the other likely connections between p─Бdas a and b favor this closer nexus.

The next questions arise because of the opening of p─Бda b, ├бtyo n├б yaс╣Гsat.

The simile goes semantically most naturally with the preceding p─Бda, тАЬlike a steed, it speeds тАж,тАЭ but the lack of accent on yaс╣Гsat makes that impossible because this verb would then be initial in its clause. The situation is complicated by the fact that yaс╣Гsat exactly replicates yaс╣Гsat in 3b, where it governs ┼Ыl├│kam in the accusative, whereas here a nominative ┼Ыl├│kaс╕е is subject of the preceding p─Бda and in order to get it to be object of yaс╣Гsat here, the subject has to change and an unexpressed acc. *┼Ыl├│kam be supplied. Moreover, the steed in the opening of b is a very likely object of yaс╣Гsat, but is in the wrong case. There are several (ad hoc) ways to handle this problem. The first is simply to interpret the text as given, with the steed compared to the subject of yaс╣Гsat, who is probably Bс╣Ыhaspati. This is in fact the interpr. of the standard tr., though each one needs to supply material and adjust interpr. in order to make it work semantically. I do not find these various makeshifts satisfactory. In order to confront the semantic problems noted above, it is possible to assume that the verb in 4b was originally really accented *y├бmс╣гat, which lost its accent redactionally because of yaс╣Гsat in the preceding verse. This would allow the tr. тАЬWhen his signal-call speeds in heaven and on earth like a steed, he will control it [=signal call/steed],тАЭ with the simile taken with p─Бda a and a new clause beginning with *y├бс╣Гsat. This may be the simplest solution, though it is not exactly the one in the published translation Instead there I (more or less) follow the suggestion sketched out by Oldenberg and discussed in more detail by Scarlatta (371 and n. 516), whereby ├бtyo n├б stands for *├бtyaс╣Г n├б; Oldenberg explains the nom. as attraction to the preceding p─Бda. Scarlatta seems to endorse OldenbergтАЩs attraction hypothesis, but his tr. is more complex (and essentially identical to mine), in that he reads the simile both as nom. with p─Бda a and (in brackets) as acc. with p─Бda b. Although this may seem over-fussy, it addresses both the syntactic and the semantic problems.

The second hemistich presents a more conventional type of double reading, whereby the word het├бyaс╕е is taken to belong both to the simile and to the frame, which its position in the p─Бda facilitates. In the frame het├н- has its common meaning тАШmissile, lanceтАЩ, a development from the general тАШimpelтАЩ meaning of тИЪhi; there is a further metaphorical development here: the missiles of Bс╣Ыhaspati are his words. In the simile, with the gen. mс╣Ыg─Б╠Бс╣З─Бm, the het├н- are the charges or drives of the wild beasts, using a more abstract or etymological sense of the -t├н-stem. This double interpr. is found in Oldenberg, Renou, and Scarlatta; it seems significantly more satisfying that GeldnerтАЩs notion (fld by Witzel Got┼Н) that takes mс╣Ыg─Б╠Бс╣З─Бm as a datival gen. – the missiles/weapons for the wild beasts – which requires that the two genitives mс╣Ыg─Б╠Бс╣З─Бm and bс╣Ы╠Бhasp├бteс╕е be non-parallel.

With Scarlatta I take the ca in c as coordinating cd with a.

I do not understand exactly what yakс╣гa-bhс╣Ы╠Бt- in b refers to, nor do I understand why the heavens are ├бhim─Бya-. For the latter, one can recall that in V.40.6, 8 the m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е of Svarbh─Бnu hide the sun and that in my extensive treatment of the Svarbh─Бnu myth (Ravenous Hyenas, 1991) I interpret those m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е as the swirling clouds of smoke issuing from Agni. So here the тАЬserpentine wilesтАЭ that the heavens possess might be the clouds of smoke from the ritual fire produced at the same time as Bс╣ЫhaspatiтАЩs ritual signal call (though ├бhim─Бya- when applied to the gods would have to have a different sense). This further suggests that the wondrous apparitions (yakс╣г├б-) that Bс╣Ыhaspati brings are other marvelous sights associated with the sacrificial performance. But these are just guesses.

Griffith

His song of praise pervades the earth and heaven: let the wise worshipper draw it, like a courser.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Bс╣Ыhaspati, you do not bestow desired (wealth) upon those stupid (men), who, sinful and mean subsist, considering you, who are auspicious, as an old ox; but you favour him who offers (you) libations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As an old ox: tv─Б usriyam manyam─Бnaс╕е: usriya = a cow giving little milk; or an old one, j─лrс╣Зam anaс╕Нv─Бham v─Б; but your favour: cayasa it piy─Бrum, you go to bestow favour on him who sacrifices with the Soma; another interpretation: you destroy the malevolent (Nirukta 4.25)

Jamison Brereton

Those who are wicked and tough, who live off you who are good, taking you for a ruddy little bullock, o godтАФ
to the evil-minded one you do not concede anything of value; you just punish the reviler, Br╠еhaspati.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take pajr─Б╠Бс╕е as a PN, as it can be elsewhere, but there seems no reason to drag in Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs kin for vilification, and I prefer taking it as a simple descriptor.

The hapax usrik├б- is a nice example of a -ka-suffixed form in slangy and deprecatory context. See my article on -ka- (IIJ 52, 2009).

There is disharmony in number between the two hemistichs: the relative cl. in the plural describing the evil rivals is picked up by dat. singular d┼лс╕Нhy├и.

The accent on c├бyase is probably due to the following ├нd, which does condition verbal accent – though in fewer passages than listed by Grassmann (s.v. ├нd 5), since many of his exx. are p─Бda-initial. It can also be noted here that the verb immediately follows a p─Бda-initial voc. and is contrastive with ├бnu dad─Бsi in c, either of which would also favor verbal accent.

Griffith

Those, God, who count thee as a worthless bullock, and, wealthy sinners, live on thee the Bounteous,–
On fools like these no blessing thou bestowest: Brhaspati, thou punishest the spiteful.

Geldner

Da die Pajra┬┤s dich f├╝r ein ├Цchslein halten und die B├╢sen dich, den Guten, ausnutzen, o Gott. So gestehst du dem B├╢sgesinnten nicht den Gewinn zu. Du strafst vielmehr den Feindseligen, o Brihaspati.

Grassmann

Den B├╢sen, die dem Oechslein gleich dich achten, und ├╝ppig von dem eignen Reichthum schwelgen, Dem Schlechten nicht, o Gott, gew├дhrst du Sch├дtze, und du bestrafst, Brihaspati, den Sp├╢tter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe a (plural asant) way to him who goes well and makes good offerings, like the affectionate friend of (a ruler who) restrains the bad; and may those sinless men who instrumental uct us, although yet enveloped (by ignorance), stand extricated from their covering.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those sinless men: abhi ye cakс╣гate naс╕е, those who speak to us; who, bodhayant─л, waken or instrumental uct us;; ap─лvс╣Ыt─Б, aj├▒─Бnen─Бvс╣Ыt─Б, enveloped by ignorance; let those who revileus, and are being protected be deprived of that protection

Jamison Brereton

(You are) easy to approach like a path leading to good pastures, but difficult to hold onto like an ally gratified by (all those) around.
The unassailable ones who watch over us have taken their stand,
unclosing the enclosed (cows).

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b the point is presumably that an ally who is constantly solicited by everyone around is likely to change sides without warning.

With Oldenberg, Renou, and Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra) I supply тАШcowsтАЩ with ├бp─лvс╣Ыt─Б(с╕е), while Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) opt for тАШdoorsтАЩ. Since they all take the Aс╣Еgirases as the implied subject, both interpr. refer to the Vala myth.

Griffith

Like a fair path is he, where grass is pleasant, though hard to win, a Friend beloved most early.
Those who unharmed by enemies behold us, while they would make them bare, stood closely compassed.

Geldner

Gern aufgesucht wie eine Stra├Яe mit sch├╢ner Weide, schwer festzuhalten wie ein umschmeichelter Freund - Die Unerreichbaren, die auf uns sehen, die sind dagestanden, indem sie die verschlossenen Tore aufschlossen.

Grassmann

Dem sch├╢n gebahnten, wiesenreichen Pfade, dem lieben Freunde gleichst du, bist unhemmbar; Die uns beschaun, die ewig unbesiegten, erhoben sich enth├╝llend das verh├╝llte.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo whom praises (necessarily) proceed, as men (assemble round a master); as rivers, rolling between their banks, flow to the ocean; that wise Bс╣Ыhaspati greedy (after rain), and stationary in the midst, contemplates both (the ferry and the water).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That wise Bс╣Ыhaspati: ubhayam caс╣гс╣нe antam. bс╣Ыhaspatistara ─Бpa┼Ыca gс╣Ыdhraс╕е: gс╣Ыdhraс╕е = vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нim ─Бk─Бс╣Еkс╣гam─Бс╣Зa, desirous of rain;

Taras = taraс╣Зam jal─Бbhivс╣Ыddhim, crossing, or a ferry or increase of water;

Apaс╕е =water; ubhayam antar madhye sthitv─Б, having stood in the middle; caс╣гс╣нe pa┼Ыyate,he sees; or karoti, he does; identifying Bс╣Ыhaspati with Indra, ubhayam, both, may denote heaven and earth, between which in the antarikс╣гa or firmament, the region of the rain, is his proper station

Jamison Brereton

On whom the chants, like streams, converge, like rivers on the sea with their banks as wheels,
Br╠еhaspati, the knowing one, gazes between both, the ford and the waters, (like) a bird of prey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The bahuvr─лhi r├│dha-cakra-, lit. тАШhaving their banks as wheelsтАЩ, may seem slightly jarring, and Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) attenuate the sense to тАЬdie die Ufer entlang rollen.тАЭ But cakr├б- is definitely the noun тАШwheelтАЩ (all the way back into PIE), not a transparent derivative of a verbal root meaning тАШrollтАЩ, and I think the cmpd must be taken in its literal sense. (So also Renou: тАЬayant pour roues les hautes-rives.тАЭ) The point of comparison must be not the speed or movement of the chariot but its physical configuration, with the wheels defining the outer limits of the vehicle as seen from above or behind and rising above the bottom of its body, just as river banks do the river.

A different watery image is found in the 2nd hemistich. With Geldner I take t├бraс╕е here as a ford (like the etymologically related t─лrth├б-, both to тИЪtс╣Э тАШcross, pass,тАЩ etc.) or perhaps more generally a means of crossing (water). Bс╣Ыhaspati, likened to a bird of prey, keeps his eye on both the ford and the (deeper) waters – presumably watching for fish to swim into the shallow water of the ford, so they can be snatched close to the surface. This image is highly reminiscent of the feeding behavior of water birds like cranes, egrets, and herons, whose preternatural stillness and singleminded vigilance as they stand in shallow water waiting for prey, followed by a swift but graceful lunge with their beaks, can only impress the observer and could well provide a model for the тАЬknowing Bс╣ЫhaspatiтАЭ and his sharp eyes depicted here. (For those who havenтАЩt had the pleasure of seeing this in the wild, there are numerous YouTube videos.) Such birds are found in the appropriate geographical areas of NW India/Pakistan, and since gс╣Ы╠Бdhra- lit. means тАШgreedyтАЩ, it need not specifically designate a vulture, pace Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), Schmidt (тАШGeierтАЩ), and Renou (тАШvautourтАЩ).

─Б╠Бpaс╕е here must be acc. pl., one of the handful of examples of the spread of the nom. pl. to acc. function in this stem.

Griffith

He to whom songs of praise go forth like torrents, as rivers eddying under banks flow sea-ward–
Brhaspati the wise, the eager, closely looks upon both, the waters and the vessel.

Dem die Ges├дnge wie Fl├╝sse zustr├╢men, wie dem Meere die Str├╢me, die die Ufer entlang rollen - Brihaspati ersp├дht als Kundiger beides, die Furt und das Wasser, der Geier.

Grassmann

Zu ihm gehn Lieder wie ins Meer die Fl├╝sse, wie Str├╢me die am Ufer sp├╝lend rollen, Und beides schaut Brihaspati, der weise, begierig hier das Schiff und die Gew├дsser.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSo, Bс╣Ыhaspati, the mighty, be beneficent, the powerful, the showerer (of benefits), the divine, has been glorified; praised by us, may he make us possessed of progeny and cattle, that hence we may obtain food, strength and long life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just so has the great, powerful one, powerfully born, the bull Br╠еhaspati, the god, been established in his place.
When praised, let him establish for us what brings heroes and cows.
тАУ May we know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. take dev├бс╕е as a predicate nominative (vel sim.) with dh─Бyi (e.g., Renou тАЬтАж a ├йt├й install├й (comme) dieuтАЭ). This may be correct, but it does assume that Bс╣Ыhaspati only secondarily came to be considered as, or was made into, a deva (so, e.g., Geldner n. 2d). Following H.-P. SchmidtтАЩs hypothesis that bс╣Ы╠Бhasp├бti- was originally an epithet of, and aspect of, Indra, it would be possible to interpret this passage as referring to the moment when Bс╣Ыhaspati emerged as a deva in his own right; on the other hand, since Indra is most definitely a deva from the beginning, a particular aspect of him should not require promotion to deva-status. It should be noted that Schmidt explicitly disputes the standard interp. (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, 75-77) and tr. dev├бс╕е as a simple descriptor: тАЬSo wird der grosse, machtgeborene, m├дchtige B., der Stier, der Gott eingesetzt.тАЭ I follow Schmidt.

Griffith

So hath Brhaspati, great, strong and mighty, the God exceeding powerful, been brought hither.
May he thus lauded give us kine and horses. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Geldner

So wurde der gro├Яe, starkgeartete, gewaltige Brihaspati, der Bulle, zum Gott eingesetzt. Er soll uns, gepriesen, den Besitz von S├╢hnen und Rindern bringen. - Wir haben vertrauliche Worte vor ihm gesprochen, ich, der Sohn des Mana, vor dem m├дchtigen Agni. Wir wollen mit den Rishis Tausend verdienen, - Wir m├╢chten einen gastlichen Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Grassmann

So ist der grosse, hochgeborne, starke Brihaspati als Gott gesetzt und Herrscher, Uns schenk der hehre Gut an Rind und Mannschaft. Gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрд╡) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдпреЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рдЪреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдорд╣рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН (рддреБрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддрдГ) рддреБрд╡реЗрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд╛рддреНрдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдГ (рддреБрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН) рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рдмреГрд╣рддрд╛рдВ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдирд╛рдордзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдиреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛ (рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рд░реЛрдордгрд┐рдГ (рдзрд╛рдпрд┐) рдзреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрддрдордГ (рд╕рдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рд╡реАрд░рд╡рддреН) рдмрд╣рд╡реЛ рд╡реАрд░рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗ рддрддреН (рдзрд╛рддреБ) рджрдзрд╛рддреБ (рдЧреЛрдорддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛ рдЧреМрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрддреН (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рее рео рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рдХрд▓рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдирдГ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрдирд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛ рдпрддрд╕реНрддреЗ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпреБрдГ рее рео реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ реердЗрддрд┐ рдирд╡рддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдЪреЗ рдорд░реНрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдкрдЯрд╡реВрди рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╕рдВрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рддреЗ рд╢рд╛рд░реАрд░рд┐рдХ рд╡ рдЖрддреНрдорд┐рдХ рдмрд▓ рд╡ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддреАрд▓. рее
